**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# ArangoDB Authentication and Authorization Audit

## Your Task

Audit the authentication and authorization infrastructure in ArangoDB. Find all C++ source files in `arangodb/arangodb` that implement auth: 1. The file under `arangod/Auth/` or `arangod/RestHandler/` that implements user authentication (look for `AuthenticationHandler` or `UserManager`). 2. The file that implements JWT token validation for the REST API. 3. The file that defines `ExecContext` or the authorization context that checks permissions for database operations. 4. The file under `arangod/RestHandler/` that implements the `/_api/user` REST endpoint for user management. 5. The configuration file or source that defines default authentication settings (`arangosh` or `arangod` startup options). Report each file path and key class/function.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/arangodb--a5cca0b8` (arangodb/arangodb)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

68-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive audit of ArangoDB's authentication and authorization infrastructure. Here's what I've documented:

## Audit Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with a complete analysis of ArangoDB's authentication and authorization system, covering:

### 5 Core Components:

1. **User Authentication** (`arangod/Auth/UserManager*`)
   - `UserManager` interface and `UserManagerImpl` implementation
   - User credential validation, password hashing, access token management
   - Database and collection-level permission resolution

2. **JWT Token Validation** (`arangod/Auth/TokenCache.*`)
   - JWT parsing and signature validation (HMAC-SHA256 and ES256)
   - Token caching with expiration
   - Basic HTTP Auth support

3. **Authorization Context** (`arangod/Utils/ExecContext.*`)
   - Thread-local execution context tracking current user permissions
   - Database and collection-level access checks
   - Admin and superuser privilege tracking

4. **REST API User Management** (`arangod/RestHandler/RestUsersHandler.*`)
   - `/_api/user` endpoints for user CRUD operations
   - Token generation (`/_open/auth`)
   - Access token management (`/_api/user/{name}/token`)
   - Auth reload (`/_admin/auth/reload`)

5. **Authentication Configuration** (`arangod/GeneralServer/AuthenticationFeature.*` and `AuthenticationOptions.h`)
   - JWT secret management (active + passive for key rotation)
   - Session timeout configuration
   - Unix socket authentication
   - External RBAC service support

### Key Additional Files:
- **HTTP Auth Processing**: `arangod/GeneralServer/CommTask.cpp` - `checkAuthHeader()` method
- **Permission Levels**: `arangod/Auth/Common.h` - NONE/RO/RW access levels
- **Handler Interface**: `arangod/Auth/Handler.h` - Extensible RBAC handler

Authorization Context (ExecContext)\\n\\n**Primary Files:** `arangod/Utils/ExecContext.h` and `arangod/Utils/ExecContext.cpp`\\n\\n- **Class:** `ExecContext` - Represents the current execution context with permission checks\\n- **Key Methods:**\\n  - `systemAuthLevel()` - Returns access level on `_system` database\\n  - `databaseAuthLevel()` - Returns access level on current database\\n  - `user()` - Returns current username\\n  - `database()` - Returns current database name\\n  - `roles()` - Returns JWT roles\\n  - `jwtToken()` - Returns JWT token if authenticated via JWT\\n\\n- **Thread-Local Storage:** `ExecContext::CURRENT` - Thread-local singleton for current execution context\\n- **Supporting Classes:**\\n  - `ExecContextScope` - RAII guard for context switching\\n  - `ExecContextSuperuserScope` - Temporarily elevate to superuser privileges\\n\\n### 4. /_api/user REST Endpoint\\n\\n**Primary Files:** `arangod/RestHandler/RestUsersHandler.h` and `.cpp`\\n\\n- **Class:** `RestUsersHandler` - HTTP Request Authentication Processing\\n\\n**Primary Files:** `arangod/GeneralServer/CommTask.cpp` and `arangod/GeneralServer/CommTask.h`\\n\\n- **Authentication Handler Method:** `CommTask::checkAuthHeader(GeneralRequest&, ServerState::Mode)`\\n- **Processing Flow:**\\n  1. Parses `Authorization` HTTP header\\n  2. Detects authentication method: `Basic` or `Bearer` (JWT)\\n  3. Calls `TokenCache::checkAuthentication()` to validate credentials\\n  4. Sets authentication result on the request object\\n  5. Records authentication events (success/failure)\\n\\n- **Key Constants:** `pathPrefixApiUser` = `\\\"/_api/user/\\\"` (special handling for user endpoints)\\n- **Startup Mode:** During startup, only JWT authentication is accepted (line 1007)\\n\\n### 7. Authentication Handler Interface (for RBAC)\\n\\n**Primary File:** `arangod/Auth/Handler.h`\\n\\n- **Class:** `Handler` (abstract) - Extensible authentication handler interface\\n- **Key Methods:**\\n  - `authenticate(username, password)` - Validate credentials and get roles\\n  - `readPermissions(username)` - Fetch permissions for already-authenticated user\\n  - `refreshRate()` - How often to refresh cached data\\n  - `allowOfflineCacheUsage()` - Whether to accept stale cache during outages\\n- **Returns:** `HandlerResult` with success/error and roles set\\n\\n### Architecture Summary\\n\\nThe authentication and authorization flow:\\n1. **HTTP Request arrives** \u2192 `CommTask::checkAuthHeader()` parses Authorization header\\n2. **Token Validation** \u2192 `TokenCache::checkAuthentication()` validates credentials (Basic or JWT)\\n3. **JWT Processing** \u2192 `TokenCache::checkAuthenticationJWT()` parses and validates JWT signature\\n4. **User Lookup** \u2192 `UserManager::checkCredentials()` verifies user exists and permissions\\n5. **ExecContext Creation** \u2192 Request context is populated with `ExecContext` containing user/roles\\n6. **Request Processing** \u2192 Handlers check permissions via `ExecContext::canUseDatabase()`, `canUseCollection()`\\n7. **User Management** \u2192 `RestUsersHandler` provides REST API for CRUD operations on users\\n\\nKey security features:\\n- Password hashing with salt\\n- JWT signature validation (HMAC-SHA256 and ES256 support)\\n- Token caching with expiration\\n- Database and collection-level permissions\\n- Admin user flag for privilege escalation\\n- Support for passive JWT secrets (key rotation)\\n- Session timeout enforcement\\n- Audit logging for authentication events\"\n}\n",

User Authentication Implementation\\n\\n**Primary File:** `arangod/Auth/UserManager.h` (interface) and `arangod/Auth/UserManagerImpl.h`/`.cpp` (implementation)\\n\\n- **Class:** `UserManager` (abstract interface) and `UserManagerImpl` (concrete implementation)\\n- **Key Methods:**\\n  - `checkCredentials(username, token)` - Validates user credentials (password or access token)\\n  - `databaseAuthLevel(username, dbname)` - Determines user's access level for a database\\n  - `collectionAuthLevel(username, dbname, collection)` - Determines access level for a collection\\n  - `storeUser(user, password, active, extras)` - Creates/updates user accounts\\n  - `loadUserCacheAndStartUpdateThread()` - Initializes user cache from `_system/_users` collection\\n  - `createAccessToken(user, name, validUntil)` - Generates access tokens for API authentication\\n\\n- **Supporting File:** `arangod/Auth/User.h` - Represents individual user entries with permissions\\n  - Stores password hashes using salted hashing\\n  - Manages database and collection-level access grants\\n  - Stores roles (Enterprise feature)\\n\\n### 2. JWT Token Validation for REST API\\n\\n**Primary Files:** `arangod/Auth/TokenCache.h` and `arangod/Auth/TokenCache.cpp`\\n\\n- **Class:** `TokenCache` - Caches authentication tokens (both Basic Auth and JWT)\\n- **Key JWT Validation Methods:**\\n  - `checkAuthenticationJWT(token)` - Main entry point for JWT validation\\n  - `validateJwtBody(bodyWebBase64)` - Parses and validates JWT claims\\n  - `validateJwtHMAC256Signature(message, signature)` - Validates HMAC-SHA256 signatures\\n  - `validateJwtES256Signature(message, signature)` - Validates ES256 (ECDSA) signatures\\n  - `validateJwtHeader(headerWebBase64)` - Validates JWT header (algorithm check)\\n  - `setJwtSecrets(active, passive, isES256)` - Manages active and passive JWT signing keys\\n  - `jwtToken()` - Returns the cached superuser JWT token for internal communication\\n\\n- **Entry Structure:** `TokenCache::Entry` - Represents cached authentication result with:\\n  - `username()` - Authenticated user\\n  - `authenticated()` - Whether authentication succeeded\\n  - `expiry()` - Token expiration time\\n  - `roles()` - JWT roles (from token claims)\\n  - `jwtToken()` - Full JWT string for re-transmission\\n\\n### 3. Authorization Context (ExecContext)\\n\\n**Primary Files:** `arangod/Utils/ExecContext.h` and `arangod/Utils/ExecContext.cpp`\\n\\n- **Class:** `ExecContext` - Represents the current execution context with permission checks\\n- **Key Methods:**\\n  - `canUseDatabase(auth::Level)` - Checks if current user can access a database\\n  - `canUseCollection(collection, auth::Level)` - Checks collection-level permissions\\n  - `collectionAuthLevel(dbname, collection)` - Returns user's access level for collection\\n  - `isAdminUser()` - Checks if user has admin privileges\\n  - `isSuperuser()` - Checks for internal superuser status\\n  - `isInternal()` - Checks if this is an internal operation\\n  - `systemAuthLevel()` - Returns access level on `_system` database\\n  - `databaseAuthLevel()` - Returns access level on current database\\n  - `user()` - Returns current username\\n  - `database()` - Returns current database name\\n  - `roles()` - Returns JWT roles\\n  - `jwtToken()` - Returns JWT token if authenticated via JWT\\n\\n- **Thread-Local Storage:** `ExecContext::CURRENT` - Thread-local singleton for current execution context\\n- **Supporting Classes:**\\n  - `ExecContextScope` - RAII guard for context switching\\n  - `ExecContextSuperuserScope` - Temporarily elevate to superuser privileges\\n\\n### 4. /_api/user REST Endpoint\\n\\n**Primary Files:** `arangod/RestHandler/RestUsersHandler.h` and `.cpp`\\n\\n- **Class:** `RestUsersHandler` - Authentication Settings and Configuration\\n\\n**Primary Files:** `arangod/GeneralServer/AuthenticationFeature.h`/`.cpp` and `arangod/GeneralServer/AuthenticationOptions.h`\\n\\n- **Class:** `AuthenticationFeature` (ApplicationFeature) - Central authentication service\\n- **Key Methods:**\\n  - `instance()` - Returns singleton instance\\n  - `isActive()` - Whether authentication is enabled\\n  - `tokenCache()` - Returns the token cache for validation\\n  - `userManager()` - Returns the user manager singleton\\n  - `hasUserdefinedJwt()` - Checks if JWT secret is configured\\n  - `jwtSecrets()` - Returns active and passive JWT secrets\\n  - `loadJwtSecretsFromFile()` - Loads JWT keys from filesystem\\n  - `sessionTimeout()` - Returns session timeout in seconds\\n  - `minimalJwtExpiryTime()` and `maximalJwtExpiryTime()` - Token lifetime bounds\\n\\n- **Configuration Structure:** `AuthenticationOptions` (struct) with defaults:\\n  - `authenticationUnixSockets = true` - Enable auth on Unix sockets\\n  - `authenticationSystemOnly = true` - Require auth for system db operations\\n  - `active = true` - Authentication enabled\\n  - `externalRBACservice = \\\"\\\"` - External RBAC handler (empty = disabled)\\n  - `sessionTimeout = 3600` - Default session timeout (1 hour, in seconds)\\n  - `minimalJwtExpiryTime = 10` - Minimum JWT expiry (10 seconds)\\n  - `maximalJwtExpiryTime = 3600` - Maximum JWT expiry (1 hour, in seconds)\\n  - `jwtSecretProgramOption` - Active JWT signing secret\\n  - `jwtSecretKeyfileProgramOption` - Path to JWT secret file\\n  - `jwtSecretFolderProgramOption` - Path to JWT secrets folder\\n  - `jwtSecretIsES256 = false` - Whether active secret uses ES256 (vs HMAC)\\n  - `jwtPassiveSecrets` - Passive secrets for verification only (Enterprise)\\n\\n### 6. HTTP Request Authentication Processing\\n\\n**Primary Files:** `arangod/GeneralServer/CommTask.cpp` and `arangod/GeneralServer/CommTask.h`\\n\\n- **Authentication Handler Method:** `CommTask::checkAuthHeader(GeneralRequest&, ServerState::Mode)`\\n- **Processing Flow:**\\n  1. Parses `Authorization` HTTP header\\n  2. Detects authentication method: `Basic` or `Bearer` (JWT)\\n  3. Calls `TokenCache::checkAuthentication()` to validate credentials\\n  4. Sets authentication result on the request object\\n  5. Records authentication events (success/failure)\\n\\n- **Key Constants:** `pathPrefixApiUser` = `\\\"/_api/user/\\\"` (special handling for user endpoints)\\n- **Startup Mode:** During startup, only JWT authentication is accepted (line 1007)\\n\\n### 7. Authentication Handler Interface (for RBAC)\\n\\n**Primary File:** `arangod/Auth/Handler.h`\\n\\n- **Class:** `Handler` (abstract) - Extensible authentication handler interface\\n- **Key Methods:**\\n  - `authenticate(username, password)` - Validate credentials and get roles\\n  - `readPermissions(username)` - Fetch permissions for already-authenticated user\\n  - `refreshRate()` - How often to refresh cached data\\n  - `allowOfflineCacheUsage()` - Whether to accept stale cache during outages\\n- **Returns:** `HandlerResult` with success/error and roles set\\n\\n### Architecture Summary\\n\\nThe authentication and authorization flow:\\n1. **HTTP Request arrives** \u2192 `CommTask::checkAuthHeader()` parses Authorization header\\n2. **Token Validation** \u2192 `TokenCache::checkAuthentication()` validates credentials (Basic or JWT)\\n3. **JWT Processing** \u2192 `TokenCache::checkAuthenticationJWT()` parses and validates JWT signature\\n4. **User Lookup** \u2192 `UserManager::checkCredentials()` verifies user exists and permissions\\n5. **ExecContext Creation** \u2192 Request context is populated with `ExecContext` containing user/roles\\n6. **Request Processing** \u2192 Handlers check permissions via `ExecContext::canUseDatabase()`, `canUseCollection()`\\n7. **User Management** \u2192 `RestUsersHandler` provides REST API for CRUD operations on users\\n\\nKey security features:\\n- Password hashing with salt\\n- JWT signature validation (HMAC-SHA256 and ES256 support)\\n- Token caching with expiration\\n- Database and collection-level permissions\\n- Admin user flag for privilege escalation\\n- Support for passive JWT secrets (key rotation)\\n- Session timeout enforcement\\n- Audit logging for authentication events\"\n}\n",
